<Review>I was invited to a Yelp Elite event...boy am I so grateful.  I was able to try a new drink that was absolutely wonderful.

This place is located on S street in Midtown between 18th and 19th street in the same location as Safeway.

As I looked over the menu I decided to order the Okinawa Oreo with boba. It comes with Japanese brown sugar milkshake with oreo.

The flavor was out of this world...the brown sugar coupled with the oreo...I would have never dreamed these two flavors would go so well together. As soon as I took my first sip...I was in dream land...wow wow wow.

I have had boba drinks before...but this one is the best I ever had flavor wise.

The boba was fresh...they have so many other things to choose from I'd your looking for milk too or ube coffee...Panna cotta...coffee drinks or tea drinks.

They also have topping choices or different boba choices such as honey boba...egg pudding...coffee jelly or panda Jelly..  as well as others.

<Rate>4</Rate>< review>
Typically a family oriented restaurant with friendly staff and regulars that visit frequently to sit comfortably and enjoy a delicious Nicaraguan meal.  Every known favorite dish is available on the menu.  The wait is considerably long, but worth it. The only downfall that I can honestly say is that Sunday's music plays a bit too loud, and found myself having to raise my voice above the comfort zone to be heard.  Overall, I recommend Rinconcito Nicaraguense for your next Nicaraguan Food cravings.< /review>

<text>TL;DR - Amazing staff, amazing quality of work, just awesome!

I ended up at La Jolla Family Smile Design after another dentist botched a crown. A friend referred me and when I walked through the door, I knew I was in the right place.

Firstly, the front desk staff was very nice and friendly upon check in. Once taken back for my initial exam and cleaning, I settled into a comfy chair in front of a big window that looked out on La Jolla. Instantly comfortable.

The cleaning and exam began, my hygienist was friendly and not too talkative, which I appreciated.

Ok, so here's where I really noticed a big difference from every other practice I've been to. As my hygienist is working on my teeth, ANOTHER dental assistant (please forgive me for using the wrong title if I am) stopped in to ask my hygienist if she needed anything. I was floored. I think that they have a "floater" staff member who visits all of the areas to make sure everything is running smoothly.

I then had my meeting with Dr. Breziner. He is the consummate professional. His calm demeanor immediately put me at ease. He walked me through the process of how they were going to fixed my botched crown (again the botched crown was from another dental office) and I would be receiving a dental implant. He said it would take about a year.

Throughout the process, I had a very positive with Dr. Fern, the oral surgeon who did the majority of the work on my implant. He is fun and kept things light hearted during the process.

Over the course of this nearly year long experience, I visited La Jolla Family Smile Design about 6 times. EVERY TIME, I was treated professionally and I felt as though my time was valued. Their billing department worked with me to help get some coverage on the tooth, because insurance companies typically do not allow you to bill on the same tooth...anyhow, the billing department's hard work helped me save about $1000.

Well here we are at the end of the process. It takes close to a year for the whole dental implant process to be completed. Today I was fitted with my permanent dental implant. It fits perfectly. I have my smile back!

Thank you to the entire staff at La Jolla Family Smile Design, you went above and beyond to make sure that I was informed, the timeline was met, and that the service was amazing!!!!< /text><Pictures>None< /Pictures>< response>

<text>I could not recommend La Jolla Family Smile Design more.

Ten months ago I was new to the area and needed to find a dentist because I wanted to get Invisalign done. After thoroughly researching numerous dentist offices I decided on this practice due to its excellent reviews.  Although I had extremely high expectations going in, Dr.Breziner and his staff absolutely exceeded those expectations.

Dental expertise and knowledge aside, the thing that stood out to me the most was an underlying sense of honesty.  Through out my Invisalign procedure I had absolute confidence in Dr.Breziner and his incredibly competent staff. I was told the price of the treatment at the beginning and there were no extra hidden costs. Everything was explained to me clearly and the staff were more than happy to answer all of my many questions!

Each and every staff member went above and beyond to help in any way. Dr.Breziner said my Invisalign treatment would be finished in ten months and that is exactly when it finished. After the treatment I decided to get my front two teeth evened out as they were slightly chipped. I am very particular about my teeth  so as usual I had multiple questions that were all answered in a professional manner that was still easy for me to understand.

After I decided that I wanted to get my front two teeth evened out I considered getting two other teeth evened out. Although this would have been double the price, Dr.Breziner told me that he didn't think that it would look better and recommended against it. I really appreciated his honest opinion. As usual he went the extra mile and even put a temporary attachment on all four teeth so that I could see what it looked like. His professional opinion was spot on as usual.

I recommend Invisalign to everyone who is not 100% happy with their teeth. To be completely honest you don't notice wearing them at all after about the  week. In the beginning I was convinced that everyone could see them but not one single person noticed.

My teeth look absolutely fantastic. They look far better than I could have imagined and I am delighted that I now have nice teeth forever :D< /text>< user_id>

Previous review:

This restaurant is located in the corner far from dining area. While i was walking around the mall, I saw a crowd of people lining up during lunch time so i thought they must have good food. There is seating outside and inside. There was no wait time which was good and the hostess sat us right away. The place is clean and there‚Äôs ample room for big groups. Our server was good and didn‚Äôt rush us to order. It was my first time here and there were a lot of appetizing dishes. We ordered the appetizer combo platter which includes the most popular appetizers. It comes with hummus trio, pita bread, tzatziki, falafel, and caprese. The appetizer was delicious and there‚Äôs enough food to share among 4 people.

I ordered the chicken wrap which has chicken, hummus spread, tomato, cucumber, pickles, and lettuce. You get the choice of ordering either a soup or salad. <Rate>1< /Rate><resp>None<//resp></record></dataset><record>
<Text>This is a new location, they've been open for 3 months. I would think that with several other successful locations there wouldn't be a learning curve with a new place but . . .

I don't know if I will return to this location. I love the Glendale location. The area, staff, ambience and food is much better.

First it is in the Century City Mall. Pretty cool, huh? Nope. It is in the Bloomingdales wing next to an elevator and a cement wall. No view. Nothing to look at. Kind of dreary.

Appetizer combo platter was sorely lacking. In Glendale the plate is covered with 3 kinds of hummus, falafel, caprese, salad and some pita. The food was overflowing the plate and you could just eat that and be full. Here not so much. Hummus was ok. The black bean one is not great. 3 little falafel balls, and 2 caprese stacks. And a lot of plate in between. The pesto on the caprese stacks was outstanding.

Entrees
Beef koubideh kabob was excellent with fluffy, tasty rice. The salad was un-eatable. I hate wilted gross mixed greens. Yuck!

Salmon and Brie panini was quite good. Imagine a bagel with locks but on a panini.

Tuna melt panini was really good. The balsamic glaze made the sandwich. The greens and red onions make it a stand out. It is also hearty enough to take 1/2 to go for later. It didn't get soggy.

There was a stern man, looked like he may be a manager hanging out talking to the employees one by one. No interaction with any costumers.

My husband ordered a hot tea and they give you a choice of several different kinds. But no sugar cubes ???? How could you serve a tea at a Mediterranean Persian leaning restaurant without a little something sweet? And I don't mean dessert. A couple of sugar cubes, or a zoolbia (like in Glendale). Not a good way to end a mean of kabob and rice.

I almost forgot the best most unexpected thing they have there! Baklava with ice cream !!! 2 triangles of Hot baklava with vanilla bean ice cream. I don't really care for baklava I could usually take it or leave it. But this hot baklava with ice cream is something else !

As I look at the pictures, maybe the plates are too big. Especially for the appetizer and dessert.

I will give it a little time before I come back to this location. I hope it improves because I do love Panini Grill and Kabob's other locations and I do love the Century City Mall< /Text>< user_id>

<Review>This is a good breakfast spot in Pacific Beach. It is part of the bottom floor of the Tower23 Hotel.

The upsides of the restaurant are that service is really good, the decorum and design is cool and relaxing, there is validated parking if you park in the Urban Outfitters lot next door, and you get a full view of the boardwalk and ocean.

In terms of the actual food, it is pretty good, but nothing to write home about. It's also just a tad overpriced. Don't get me wrong, the food is good and fresh, but it's basic and not totally worth the price tag. The slight price hike can be reasonably attributed to the decorum, service, and view though.

The photos attached to this review show a breakfast tea set up, the vegetarian scramble, and the avocado toast.<//Review><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN9fnZcX6aQ06AJo4HJ8WULzsJuGB7VIApqaMTf=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNDsN4SsdV5Gi0BUxGI6E98-rhYyg7c01F07H8a=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOL0GNHV4ofaDK5S2BbpIGOJyXGwv_syL_6x86s=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics>< resp>

[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOSIT5bQK1ByeO1jdPfLo0aG6RNIRaKxII5grx7=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMFB1pm-NALcKMfxcjdowtGAHEKse29Ocpye9o7=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPEW-jj957u0lk1uxAbKW7esQNm59vQnFXNEJxd=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMBlxCIBpYINEI_UUhwqz-yf5QLpA9naXdWC_gV=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</pictures>
<user_name>Jay Keyes< /user_name><text>Although Pacific Beach restaurant JRDN is ostensibly trendy, it has now been operating in San Diego since 2006, so it clearly is no longer surviving on hype alone. The restaurant has re-invented itself this past winter with a modest remodel while bringing back chef David Warner who has since evolved the already Asian-heavy Southern Californian menu to feature even more Asian dishes. While I struggle to call JRDN "fine dining," it has retained an upscale vibe and, with all due disrespect to "World Famous," JRDN is the only restaurant where one can sip a craft cocktail while enjoying anything close to a high-quality meal on Pacific Beach's concrete boardwalk.

In case you were wondering (because I was), JRDN stands for "Jordan," which is the name of the hotel owner's son and also his father, and this is important because it helps us keep mindful that JRDN is a hotel restaurant. It does not need to cater to crude local tastes but rather its culinary team has more freedom to take avant-garde risks with its menu to serve well-off guests with more worldly dining needs. Tower 23 is a "luxury hotel" with rooms that start at north of $900 per night during summer months and thus will always require an on-premises high-end restaurant regardless if the locals reject it. This leaves Chef Warner with the ability and financial flexibility to do just about anything he wants. While this setup is the reason why many chi-chi hotel restaurants are overpriced and terrible, we should note that some of San Diego's very best and most enduring restaurants (Addison, Vivace, etc.) operate in this model, which is also the basis of Las Vegas's entire fine dining scene.

"Clams with Spaghetti" is the kind of pasta dish I cannot resist ordering when I see it on menus. Here at JRDN, their dish consisted of Pernod and charred fennel, which added an unusually heavy herbal and licoricey quality to this dish unlike any variation I've previously had. They threw in Chinese sausage (i.e., pork seasoned with "5 Spice") and tomatoes, and I was served a dish that hit the mark in terms of satisfying my hunger but left me scratching my head wondering what they were trying to achieve in terms of taste.

This is why I appreciate and prefer the straightforward mouth-watering richness of the buttery, garlicky chorizo cream sauce in JRDN's new "Steamed Mussels" dish. I could pick a day and do nothing but sit on JRDN's patio with a few loaves of bread and a bottomless supply of this sauce and die a happy man from heart failure at the end of it.

Similarly, the sushi dishes at JRDN have always been pretty good, especially their "Local Yellowtail" dish of hamachi soaking in sesame mirin, enhanced by jalape√±os and garlic, served with crispy, salty taro chips - which is essentially a better version, in my opinion, of the same dish served at "Trust," whose chef used to work at JRDN. The "Nigiri" served to me across a few visits has been of sufficiently high quality, particularly their tako (octopus) which is often dry and tasteless elsewhere but has a perfect texture and pleasant flavor at JRDN.

I could write more about some of the items no longer on the menu, but I'll summarize by saying that this restaurant's range is "average to very good," with not many misses, but also not many particularly great dishes aside from the mussels. During each visit here, I always expect just a little bit better than what I get. Given the flexibility of his setup, I'd like to see Chef Warner play things a little less safe. That said, "safe" is more likely to create repeat customers. This is why, while not my first choice for dining out in San Diego, JRDN is always a reasonable option when I plan to be at Pacific Beach around lunch or dinner time.<//text>< Resp>
None</Resp>

<Rating>1< /Rating>< review>
Didn't know I was allergic to Lobster. Had an awesome meal at JRDN. Then finished the last few bites of my daughter's lobster pasta. Within seconds I passed out. No alcohol consumed. When I regained consciousness I was more dizzy than I have ever been. For some reason, one of the JRDN staff, was committed to getting me out of there quickly. He kept telling me he wanted me to go wait outside for the ambulance. I kept telling him if I didn't sit down or lay down I felt like I would vomit. This guy was sure it would be in JRDN'S best interest to get me outside for some reason. I still can't figure out why.

Thankfully, my wife helped me get to a comfortable place to lay down in the lobby. Then one conscientious employee of JRDN with EMT training helped me until the ambulance and paramedics arrived. That one guy still wanted me to go outside but he was basically told to pack sand by the professionals on the scene. It was so strange to be treated like someone who had walked into JRDN and overdosed on drugs (like a hobo on H) or drank a whole bottle of liquor and passed out. The entire staff, except for the guy with EMT training acted like we were riff raff that needed to be kicked out for disrupting the place. Our server obviously knew nobody at our table ordered any alcohol.

The manager did call my wife yesterday and apologized profusely. He ended up refunding us for the meal. Funny, because JRDN called to make sure we paid the bill while I was in the ambulance on the way to the emergency room. If you plan never to have any sudden health issues you might like eating at JRDN. But, if you're a typical human being you might want to stick to restaurants where you won't be asked to "wait on the curb" if you have an allergic reaction to food or a heart attack.</review>

<review>JRDN is an open air lounge overlooking the Pacific Ocean and PB Boardwalk where the nightly main event is the sunset over the water. A very close second would probably be the people watching on the boardwalk.

This is a swanky under the sky, happy hour, flip flop, white table cloth, nothin fussy beachfront restaurant to unwind and refuel.

Off of the raw bar menu, what could be more delicious than clams with butter or fresh oysters in their shells?

The spirit bar specializes in craft cocktails and personal wine and the offerings were solid.

All I wanted today was an outside prototypical California beach happy hour hangout where I can buy a Bombay Sapphire Martini, up, with olives and a little basket of clams.< /review>< Date>

113377672871964931289< /UserId.>
< Text>
JRDN has it all: exceptional service, a beautiful location, free valet parking right by the water, and the best food on the beach.

If you make for a weekend brunch, their bloody mary is a must, and I'm not an easy one to please when it comes to this breakfast staple.
For lunch, you can't go wrong with the lobster BLT with truffle fries (the best tasting and best priced twist on a lobster roll in PB) or the chorizo steamed mussels.
The Lobster BLT comes stacked with lobster meat on a lightly sweet grilled bread, with butter lettuce, fresh tomato, and a few delicious strips of bacon. YUM!
If you're in from out of town, you can get a room at Tower 23, with its awesome rooftop pool, and stop through JRDN for an incredible steak dinner as well.
JRDN offer the primest cuts of beef prepared to your specifications, with my favorite always including the bone marrow butter. And if you want a little surf with your turf, add a half dozen oysters on the half shell.
You can enjoy all of this right on their beachfront patio, or inside with a beautiful sunset view and spectacular service!</Text>

<date>1495504890301< /date><rate>2<//rate>< text>
(5 stars for food, 1 star for service) My best friend and I visited this restaurant on Sunday May 21st 2017 to celebrate the last night of our weekend getaway to San Diego. The food was incredible but unfortunately, we received the WORST service either of us have ever had. Our server Jaydn was incredibly rude and treated both of us horribly - by the end of the night it was obvious he was expecting a small bill/tip from us. Jaydn greeted us and returned about 15 minutes later to finally take our order. My friend started off by ordering a salad and before even asking me if I would like one, he snarkily asked if we were sharing the salad (I assumed he was hinting at the fact that we couldn't afford two salads). Next, we ordered our entrees. My friend ordered the cheapest steak and Jadyn cracked a smirk as he wrote it down. Then I ordered the atlantic Salmon and he cracked another smirk as he wrote that down as well (again probably hinting at the fact that we couldn't afford anything more expensive - seriously???). Before receiving our food my friend mentioned to him that she never received a napkin and his response was, "Oh what the hell?" Worst of all, this was the LAST we saw of our server until receiving the bill. For the rest of the night, the busser working in our section took care of us - refilling our waters, asking us how we were enjoying our meal, and even offering the desert menu and taking our desert orders. He was incredibly nice and was the only reason we even decided to stay. We finally were greeted by our server again after finishing our desert where he asked us if we would like the bill to be together or separate. After requesting to have separate bills, he nodded and without walking away, immediately handed us the bill (we assumed he already separated the check). But when we opened the tab we noticed he put it on one tab which defeated the purpose of him even asking our preference because he clearly was going to just do it the way he wanted to anyways. My friend and I still tipped 20% out of respect for the busser but I regret not complaining to a manager about our server which is why I am writing this review. At the end of the day, I would just like to thank the incredible busser for saving the day and still making our experience an enjoyable one.</text>

<user_name>Thom Cate</user_name>< Time>
1276924864044< /Time>
<rating>4</rating><Text>JRDN is not your ordinary restaurant in Mission Beach; if you want ordinary, there are a fat double-handfull of restos within walking distance of JRDN--and dinner for two-to-three at any of those will cost you what a single meal at JRDN will.

But you won't get your meal cooked to perfection.  And the cut won't be so generous.  The flavors will be pedestrian, ordinary and expected...and you'll probably have a good time and save a few bucks, right?  But you should try JRDN, at least once.

We've read some of the reviews below, and have never had a negative experience (re: Katherine, 6-10-2010) reported; we almost wonder if she was at the same JRDN, but any place can have an off night.  We too have noticed the main server is standoffish, almost cold, while the assistants are gracious, warm and helpful.

The meals tonight were the rib eye (medium rare) w/"Chef's Thunder,"an amazing reduction of onions, bleu cheese & balsamic, with Yukon gold mash & onion rings, and the seared scallops with lemon risotto and a JRDN salad (you pick a base and five ingredients from a list--fun!).  Our daughter had the "Real Mac & Cheese," but fell dead asleep after a long day; she'll enjoy it tomorrow.

Both adult dishes were straight-up perfect, with wonderful flavors and textures.  My wife is especially picky about her scallops and could not say enough good things about them. My steak was cooked to medium-rare perfection and nicely lean without being dry.

We did not order drinks, and were mildly vexed to see the "Naturo Still" water (which we did not order, but magically appeared on our table) was billed to us--despite it tasting more like tap water, and the bottle being obviously re-used. A strangely cheap note in an otherwise top-shelf performance.

Dinner for two adults and one child, no alcohol, with taxes: $103.</Text><Pics>None<//Pics><resp>None< /resp>< gmap_id>
